     1	import IOKit.pwr_mgt
     2	import XCTest
     3	@testable import Phoenix
     4	
     5	@MainActor
     6	final class KeepMacAwakeTests: XCTestCase {
     7	    private var defaults: CountingUserDefaults!
     8	    private var suiteName: String!
     9	
    10	    override func setUp() {
    11	        super.setUp()
    12	        suiteName = "KeepMacAwakeTests-\(UUID().uuidString)"
    13	        defaults = CountingUserDefaults(suiteName: suiteName)!
    14	        defaults.removePersistentDomain(forName: suiteName)
    15	    }
    16	
    17	    override func tearDown() {
    18	        defaults.removePersistentDomain(forName: suiteName)
    19	        defaults = nil
    20	        suiteName = nil
    21	        super.tearDown()
    22	    }
    23	
    24	    // Toggle ON → IOPMAssertionCreateWithName fails → isEnabled must revert to
    25	    // false, UserDefaults must persist false, acquire must be tried exactly
    26	    // once (no recursion through suppressApply), and exactly one UserDefaults
    27	    // write of the final value must occur for the toggle interaction.
    28	    func testFailedAcquireRevertsToggleAndWritesOnceWithoutRecursion() {
    29	        defaults.set(false, forKey: KeepMacAwake.preferencesKey)
    30	
    31	        var acquireCallCount = 0
    32	        let failingAcquire: KeepMacAwake.AssertionCreator = {
    33	            acquireCallCount += 1
    34	            return (kIOReturnError, IOPMAssertionID(0))
    35	        }
    36	
    37	        let keepMacAwake = KeepMacAwake(userDefaults: defaults, assertionCreator: failingAcquire)
    38	        // After init: isEnabled=false, applyEnabled goes to else branch
    39	        // (releaseAssertion no-op) and writes false to UserDefaults. Reset
    40	        // the test counters AFTER init to scope the assertions to the
    41	        // toggle interaction.
    42	        XCTAssertFalse(keepMacAwake.isEnabled)
    43	        XCTAssertEqual(acquireCallCount, 0, "init should not attempt acquire when seeded false")
    44	        defaults.resetWriteCount(forKey: KeepMacAwake.preferencesKey)
    45	
    46	        // The pre-fix code would have left isEnabled=true and UserDefaults=true
    47	        // after this assignment because the failure path silently swallowed
    48	        // the IOReturn. The post-fix code reverts both, in a single bounded
    49	        // didSet round.
    50	        keepMacAwake.isEnabled = true
    51	
    52	        XCTAssertFalse(keepMacAwake.isEnabled, "isEnabled must revert to false when acquire fails")
    53	        XCTAssertFalse(
    54	            defaults.bool(forKey: KeepMacAwake.preferencesKey),
    55	            "UserDefaults must persist the reverted false, not the user's intended true"
    56	        )
    57	        XCTAssertEqual(
    58	            acquireCallCount, 1,
    59	            "acquireAssertion must be called exactly once — suppressApply gate must prevent the inner isEnabled=false write from re-entering applyEnabled and re-invoking the closure"
    60	        )
    61	        XCTAssertEqual(
    62	            defaults.writeCount(forKey: KeepMacAwake.preferencesKey), 1,
    63	            "exactly one UserDefaults write of the resolved value (false), not one per didSet pass"
    64	        )
    65	    }
    66	
    67	    // Init-path coverage. The toggle test above never exercises init's
    68	    // explicit applyEnabled() call — if init's revert path were deleted, that
    69	    // test would still pass. This one seeds UserDefaults=true so init's
    70	    // applyEnabled is the *only* code path that runs.
    71	    func testFailedInitFromSeededTrueRevertsAndPersistsFalse() {
    72	        defaults.set(true, forKey: KeepMacAwake.preferencesKey)
    73	        defaults.resetWriteCount(forKey: KeepMacAwake.preferencesKey)
    74	
    75	        var acquireCallCount = 0
    76	        let failingAcquire: KeepMacAwake.AssertionCreator = {
    77	            acquireCallCount += 1
    78	            return (kIOReturnError, IOPMAssertionID(0))
    79	        }
    80	
    81	        let keepMacAwake = KeepMacAwake(userDefaults: defaults, assertionCreator: failingAcquire)
    82	
    83	        XCTAssertFalse(
    84	            keepMacAwake.isEnabled,
    85	            "init must revert isEnabled to false when the seeded-true UserDefaults causes acquire to be attempted and fail"
    86	        )
    87	        XCTAssertFalse(
    88	            defaults.bool(forKey: KeepMacAwake.preferencesKey),
    89	            "init must persist the reverted false to UserDefaults so the next launch reads false"
    90	        )
    91	        XCTAssertEqual(
    92	            acquireCallCount, 1,
    93	            "init's applyEnabled must call the assertion creator exactly once — not twice (recursion) and not zero (skipped init revert)"
    94	        )
    95	        XCTAssertEqual(
    96	            defaults.writeCount(forKey: KeepMacAwake.preferencesKey), 1,
    97	            "init's applyEnabled must write the final value exactly once"
    98	        )
    99	    }
   100	}
   101	
   102	/// Counts `set(_:forKey:)` invocations per key. Subclasses `UserDefaults` so
   103	/// it slots into `KeepMacAwake`'s injected dependency without a wrapper
   104	/// protocol; only the Bool overload is overridden because that's the one
   105	/// `KeepMacAwake.applyEnabled` calls.
   106	private final class CountingUserDefaults: UserDefaults {
   107	    private var counts: [String: Int] = [:]
   108	
   109	    override func set(_ value: Bool, forKey defaultName: String) {
   110	        counts[defaultName, default: 0] += 1
   111	        super.set(value, forKey: defaultName)
   112	    }
   113	
   114	    func writeCount(forKey key: String) -> Int { counts[key] ?? 0 }
   115	
   116	    func resetWriteCount(forKey key: String) { counts[key] = 0 }
   117	}

 succeeded in 0ms:
     1	# PlowD
     2	
     3	PlowD is the local FastAPI process that manages OpenClaw gateway runtime for the app.
     4	
     5	Current scope:
     6	
     7	- Start/stop OpenClaw gateway + node host
     8	- Maintain Plow guardrails for `openclaw.json` (loopback + token auth + plugin wiring)
     9	- Run operator WebSocket client for pairing and exec approval decisions
    10	- Expose PlowD status and gateway policy callbacks
    11	
    12	Known behaviors and recovery notes:
    13	
    14	- historical notes: [`../../docs/openclaw-phoenixd-known-behaviors.md`](../../docs/openclaw-phoenixd-known-behaviors.md)
    15	
    16	Script guide:
    17	
    18	- [`scripts/README.md`](scripts/README.md)
    19	- [`justfile`](justfile)
    20	
    21	## Prerequisites
    22	
    23	- `uv`
    24	
    25	## Setup
    26	
    27	```bash
    28	cd app/plowd
    29	uv sync
    30	cp .env.example .env
    31	```
    32	
    33	Edit `.env` as needed for your machine.
    34	
    35	## Running
    36	
    37	Common rule:
    38	
    39	- use the repo root [`justfile`](../../justfile) for normal app workflows
    40	- use the local [`justfile`](justfile) only when you are already working directly inside `app/plowd/`
    41	- the local daemon justfile is intentionally narrow; `just test` is the main supported entrypoint
    42	
    43	From repo root:
    44	
    45	```bash
    46	just app build
    47	just app up
    48	just app release
    49	just app logs
    50	```
    51	
    52	Server:
    53	
    54	- `http://127.0.0.1:18788`
    55	- docs: `http://127.0.0.1:18788/docs`
    56	
    57	Logs:
    58	
    59	- terminal output
    60	- appended to `~/Library/Application Support/co.plow.app/plowd.log`
    61	
    62	## Common Workflows
    63	
    64	```bash
    65	just app build        # build Swift app + package VM/runtime into the current dev app variant
    66	just app up           # rebuild Swift app, then run against repo PlowD with reload
    67	just app release      # signed release package under .build/
    68	just app logs         # tail app/plowd/vm/openclaw logs
    69	cd app/plowd && just test
    70	cd ../openclaw/channels/plow-imessage && npm run build:watch
    71	```
    72	
    73	## Fast Validation Flow
    74	
    75	Use `cd app/plowd && just test` for daemon unit coverage.
    76	
    77	Use `just app build` once to prepare the app bundle, then `just app up` for the normal local launch loop.
    78	
    79	## Active HTTP Surface
    80	
    81	- `GET /status`
    82	  - PlowD/gateway/operator readiness
    83	  - includes `agents: {}` for compatibility with existing macOS client contract
    84	- `POST /internal/gateway/policy/tool-check`
    85	- `POST /internal/gateway/policy/tool-result`
    86	
    87	## Project Structure (Current)
    88	
    89	```
    90	app/plowd/
    91	├── README.md
    92	├── justfile
    93	├── .env.example
    94	├── scripts/
    95	│   ├── README.md
    96	│   ├── plowd-stage-runtime
    97	│   ├── plowd-package-runtime
    98	│   ├── plowd-validate-package
    99	│   ├── plowd-packaged-agent

  1828	    // Exposed as `internal` (not `private`) so PhoenixTests can directly
  1829	    // exercise the claim/finish state machine for #443 regression coverage.
  1830	    func claimRuntimeLaunchIfNeeded() -> Bool {
  1831	        runtimeLaunchLock.lock()
  1832	        defer { runtimeLaunchLock.unlock() }
  1833	
  1834	        if daemonProcess?.isRunning == true || isLaunching || isRestartingRuntime {
  1835	            return false
  1836	        }
  1837	        if launchAttempts >= maxLaunchAttempts {
  1838	            appendAppLog("PlowD failed to start after \(maxLaunchAttempts) attempts.")
  1839	            Task { @MainActor in
  1840	                self.error = "PlowD failed to start after \(self.maxLaunchAttempts) attempts."
  1841	                self.runtimeLaunchState = .idle
  1842	            }
  1843	            return false
  1844	        }
  1845	
  1846	        isLaunching = true
  1847	        Task { @MainActor in
  1848	            self.runtimeLaunchState = .launching(startedAt: Date())
  1849	            self.error = nil
  1850	        }
  1851	        return true
  1852	    }
  1853	
  1854	    // Exposed as `internal` (not `private`) so PhoenixTests can directly
  1855	    // exercise the claim/finish state machine for #443 regression coverage.
  1856	    func finishClaimedRuntimeLaunch() {
  1857	        runtimeLaunchLock.lock()
  1858	        isLaunching = false
  1859	        runtimeLaunchLock.unlock()
  1860	        // Pair with claimRuntimeLaunchIfNeeded: once we stop actively launching,
  1861	        // runtimeLaunchState must leave .launching regardless of whether the
  1862	        // daemon reached .ok. Previously this transition lived only at the deep
  1863	        // success point inside the startup readiness wait loop, so a slow
  1864	        // gateway startup (recovered by the periodic status poll) left
  1865	        // isRuntimeLaunchInProgress stuck at true forever. (Bug #443.)

## [architecture] findings

### Surveyed
- Current Phoenix runtime ownership: Swift app launches and stops PlowD/VM today — clean
- `KeepMacAwake` as one `@MainActor` app-level singleton in `PhoenixAppDelegate` — clean
- IOKit assertion lifecycle and quit teardown — clean
- Installer settings placement in a separate `System` card — clean
- Status popover toggle surface — see Finding 1
- Reverted installer auto-sizing work: current PR keeps fixed installer heights — clean
- Test-only injection seam for IOKit/UserDefaults failures — clean

### Finding 1 — low
Broken-Glass Test asks: Will users normally discover and toggle Keep Mac Awake from the status popover after setup rather than from installer Settings? If yes, this PR splits one product contract across two surfaces: Settings carries the real OS constraints in the subtitle/help, but the connected status panel exposes only `Keep Mac Awake` plus a switch. A user toggling from the status panel can still expect lid-close or battery behavior the assertion cannot deliver. The low-cost remedy is to collapse to one shared row/copy or carry the same help text here; that removes contract drift without adding defensive branches.
